     <p><b>Arizona State University</b> (commonly referred to as <b>ASU</b> or <b>Arizona State</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Space_grant_colleges" title="Space grant colleges" class="mw-redirect">national space-grant</a> institution and <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> located in the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Metropolitan_Area" title="Phoenix Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Phoenix Metropolitan Area</a> of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_colleges_and_universities_by_enrollment" title="List of United States colleges and universities by enrollment">largest public university</a> in the United States by enrollment.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="ref_b" class="reference"><a href="#cnote_b">b[›]</a></sup> Founded in 1885 as the <a href="/wiki/Normal_School" title="Normal School" class="mw-redirect">Tempe Normal School</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Territory" title="Arizona Territory">Arizona Territory</a>, the school came under control of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">Arizona Board of Regents</a> in 1945 and was renamed <i>Arizona State College.</i><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> A 1958 statewide ballot measure gave the university its present name. In 1994 ASU was classified as a <a href="/wiki/Research_I" title="Research I" class="mw-redirect">Research I</a> institute; thus, making Arizona State one of the newest major research universities (public or private) in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Arizona State's mission is to create a model of the “New American University” whose efficacy is measured “by those it includes and how they succeed, not by those it excludes”.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU awards <a href="/wiki/Bachelors_degree" title="Bachelors degree" class="mw-redirect">bachelors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masters_degree" title="Masters degree" class="mw-redirect">masters</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral</a> degrees, and is broadly organized into 16 colleges and schools spread across four campuses:<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> the original <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Tempe_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Tempe campus">Tempe campus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_West_campus" title="Arizona State University at the West campus">West campus</a> in northwest <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Polytechnic_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Polytechnic campus">Polytechnic campus</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Downtown_Phoenix_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Downtown Phoenix campus">Downtown Phoenix campus</a>. All four campuses are accredited as a single institution by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Learning_Commission" title="Higher Learning Commission" class="mw-redirect">Higher Learning Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The University is categorized as a Research University with very high research activity (RU/VH) as reported by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> with a research expenditure of $385 million in 2012. Arizona State is one of the appointed members of the <a href="/wiki/Universities_Research_Association" title="Universities Research Association">Universities Research Association</a>, a consortium of 86 leading research-oriented universities.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU's athletic teams compete in <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> and are collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Sun_Devils" title="Arizona State Sun Devils">Arizona State Sun Devils</a>. They are members of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a> and have won 23 national championships. Along with multiple athletic clubs and recreational facilities, ASU is also home to over 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Student_society" title="Student society">registered student organizations</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> across its campuses, reflecting the diversity of the student body. With the continued growth of the student population, ASU has recently undergone numerous renovations across each of its campuses, including expansion of athletic facilities, student recreational centers and <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">dormitories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The demand for improved facilities and more student housing on campus is being addressed with public/private investment.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, ASU campus housing accommodates one of the largest residential populations in the nation with over 13,000 residents,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> a figure that will increase each year as the university continues to build more <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">on-campus housing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc">

       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <div id="toctitle">

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Arizona_State_University" title="History of Arizona State University">History of Arizona State University</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/66/Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg/250px-Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg" width="250" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/66/Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg/375px-Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/66/Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg/500px-Pres._Theodore_Roosevelt_at_Old_Main_of_Arizona_State_University.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">

        </div> Old Main on the Arizona State University campus, circa 1890

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1885.E2.80.931929">1885–1929</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1885–1929">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Originally named the <i>Tempe Normal School</i>, the institution was founded on March 12, 1885, after John Samuel Armstrong first introduced House Bill 164, &quot;An Act to Establish a <a href="/wiki/Normal_school" title="Normal school">Normal school</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Arizona" title="Territory of Arizona" class="mw-redirect">Territory of Arizona</a> to the <a href="/wiki/13th_Arizona_Territorial_Legislature" title="13th Arizona Territorial Legislature">13th Legislative Assembly</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Territory" title="Arizona Territory">Arizona Territory</a>. Instruction was instituted on February 8, 1886 under the supervision of Principal Hiram Bradford Farmer. Land for the school was donated by <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe</a> residents George and Martha Wilson, allowing 33 students to meet in a single room.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>At the beginning of the 20th century, the school's name was changed from Tempe Normal School to the <i>Arizona State Teachers College at Tempe</i>. Before becoming a college, the <a href="/wiki/Normal_School" title="Normal School" class="mw-redirect">Normal School</a> enrolled high school students with no other secondary education facilities. Under the 30-year tenure of president Arthur John Matthews the school was given all-college student status. The first dormitories built in the state were constructed under his supervision. Of the 18 buildings constructed while Matthews was president, six are still currently in use. Matthews envisioned an &quot;evergreen campus,&quot; with many shrubbery brought to the campus. He also implemented the planting of <a href="/wiki/Palm_Walk" title="Palm Walk">Palm Walk</a>, now one of the feature landmarks of the Tempe campus. His legacy is being continued to this day with the main campus having the honor of being declared a nationally recognized arboretum.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, Ralph W. Swetman was hired as president for a three-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Although enrollment increased by almost 100% during his tenure due to the depression, many faculty were terminated and faculty salaries were cut.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1930.E2.80.931989">1930–1989</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1930–1989">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG/250px-FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG" width="250" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG/375px-FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG/500px-FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:FLW_Gammage_Auditorium_ASU_PHX_AZ_20186.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> ASU's 
        <a href="/wiki/Gammage_Auditorium" title="Gammage Auditorium" class="mw-redirect">Gammage Auditorium</a>, designed by 
        <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1933, <a href="/wiki/Grady_Gammage" title="Grady Gammage">Grady Gammage</a>, then president of Arizona State Teachers College at <a href="/wiki/Flagstaff,_Arizona" title="Flagstaff, Arizona">Flagstaff</a>, became president of <i>Arizona State Teachers College at Tempe</i>, a tenure that would last for nearly 28 years. Like his predecessor, Gammage oversaw the construction of a number of buildings on the Tempe campus. Dr. Gammage oversaw the development of the university, graduate programs, and the renaming of the <i>Arizona State College</i> to Arizona State University in 1958.</p> 
     <p>By the 1960s, with the presidency of Dr. <a href="/wiki/G._Homer_Durham" title="G. Homer Durham">G. Homer Durham</a>, Arizona State University began to expand its academic curriculum by establishing several new colleges and beginning to award <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a> and other doctoral degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The next three presidents—Harry K. Newburn, 1969–71, John W. Schwada, 1971–81, and J. Russell Nelson, 1981–89—and Interim President Richard Peck, 1989, led the university to increased academic stature, creation of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_West_campus" title="Arizona State University at the West campus">West Campus</a>, and rising enrollment.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG/220px-ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG" width="220" height="58" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG/330px-ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG/440px-ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Main_-_Barrett02_-_2009-08-28.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Example of a new academic village, taken at Barrett, The Honors College on the Tempe Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.93present">1990–present</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1990–present">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Under the leadership of Dr. Lattie F. Coor, from 1990 to June 2002, ASU grew through the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Polytechnic_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Polytechnic campus">Polytechnic campus</a> and extended education sites. His commitment to diversity, quality in <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate education</a>, research, and economic development underscored the university's significant gains in each of these areas over his 12-year tenure. Part of Dr. Coor's legacy to the university was a successful fund-raising campaign: Through private donations, more than $500 million was invested in targeted areas that would significantly impact the future of ASU. Among the campaign's achievements were the naming and endowing of <a href="/wiki/Barrett,_The_Honors_College" title="Barrett, The Honors College">Barrett, The Honors College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Herberger_College_of_the_Arts" title="Herberger College of the Arts" class="mw-redirect">Katherine K. Herberger College of Fine Arts</a>, and the Morrison School of Agribusiness and Resource Management; the creation of many new endowed faculty positions; and hundreds of new scholarships and fellowships.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asubiodesign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Asubiodesign.jpg/250px-Asubiodesign.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Asubiodesign.jpg/375px-Asubiodesign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Asubiodesign.jpg/500px-Asubiodesign.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asubiodesign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> ASU's 
        <a href="/wiki/Biodesign_Institute" title="Biodesign Institute">Biodesign Institute</a> on Tempe campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On July 1, 2002, <a href="/wiki/Michael_M._Crow" title="Michael M. Crow">Michael Crow</a> became the university's 16th president. At his inauguration, President Crow outlined his vision for transforming ASU into a &quot;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://newamericanuniversity.asu.edu/">New American University</a>&quot;—one that would be open and inclusive with a goal set for the university to meet <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU) criteria and to become a member.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Further, Crow initiated the idea of transforming ASU into &quot;One University in Many Places&quot; by merging ASU's several campuses into a single institution, sharing students, faculty, staff and accreditation. Aided by hundreds of millions of dollars in donations, ASU embarked on an aggressive years-long research facility capital building effort, resulting in the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Biodesign_Institute" title="Biodesign Institute">Biodesign Institute</a> and several large interdisciplinary research buildings. Along with the research facilities, the university faculty was expanded, including the addition of three <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureates" title="Nobel Laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Laureates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, ASU's <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Downtown_Phoenix_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Downtown Phoenix campus">Downtown Phoenix</a> campus was vastly expanded with several of the University's colleges and schools relocated to the downtown campus. Since fiscal year 2002 ASU's research expenditures have tripled and more than 1.5 million sq. ft. of new research space has been added to the university's research facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession" class="mw-redirect">economic downturn</a> that began in 2008 took a particularly hard toll on Arizona, resulting in large cuts to ASU's budget.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In response to these cuts, ASU underwent several rounds of reorganizations,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> combining academic departments, consolidating colleges and schools, and reducing university staff and administrators; however, with an economic recovery underway in 2011, ASU continued its campaign to expand the West and Polytechnic Campuses,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> and establishing a set of low-cost, teaching-focused extension campuses in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Havasu_City" title="Lake Havasu City" class="mw-redirect">Lake Havasu City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Payson,_Arizona" title="Payson, Arizona">Payson, Arizona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has announced that a new building for the Sandra Day O’Connor College of Law will be built on the Downtown Phoenix Campus, relocating faculty and students from the Tempe Campus. The university plans to establish the Arizona Center for Law and Society in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_Administration">Organization and Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Organization and Administration">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">Arizona Board of Regents</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Arizona Board of Regents governs Arizona State University as well as the other state's public universities; <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona" title="University of Arizona">University of Arizona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Arizona_University" title="Northern Arizona University">Northern Arizona University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board of Regents is composed of twelve members including eleven voting, and one non-voting member. Members of the board include the Governor and the Superintendent of Public Instruction acting as ex-officio members, eight volunteer Regent members with eight years term that are appointed by the Governor, and two Student Regents with two years term, serving a one-year term as non-voting apprentices. <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">ABOR</a> provides policy guidance to the state universities of Arizona. ASU has multiple campus locations, covering the Phoenix metropolitan areas including the Main Tempe campus in Tempe, the West campus and Downtown Phoenix campus both in Phoenix, and the Polytechnic campus in Mesa. It also offers courses and degrees through ASU online to advance the mission of the university.</p> 
     <p>The Arizona Board of Regents appoints and elects the president of the university, who is considered the chief executive officer and the chief budget officer of the institution.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The president is responsible for the execution of measures enacted by the Board of Regents, controls the property of the university, and acts as the official representative of the university to the Board of Regents.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The chief executive officer is assisted through the administration of the institution by the provost, vice presidents, deans, faculty, directors, department chairs, and other officers.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The president also selects and appoints administrative officers and general counsels. The 16th and current ASU president is Michael M. Crow, and has served since July 1, 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses_and_locations">Campuses and locations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campuses and locations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>ASU's academic programs are spread across campuses in the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Metropolitan_Area" title="Phoenix Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Phoenix Metropolitan Area</a>; however, unlike most multi-campus institutions, ASU describes itself as &quot;one university in many places,&quot; explaining that it is &quot;not a system with separate campuses, and not one main campus with branch campuses.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The university considers each campus &quot;distinctive&quot; and academically focused on certain aspects of the overall university mission. The Tempe Campus is the university's research and graduate school center. Undergraduate studies on the Tempe campus are research-based programs designed to prepare students for graduate school, professional school, or employment.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The Polytechnic campus is designed with an emphasis on professional and technological programs for direct workforce preparation. The Polytechnic campus is the location of many of the university's simulators and laboratories dedicated for project-based learning.<sup id="cite_ref-campus.asu.edu_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campus.asu.edu-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The West campus is focused on interdisciplinary degrees and the liberal arts, while maintaining professional programs with a direct impact on the community and society.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The Downtown Campus focuses on direct urban and public programs such as nursing, public policy, mass communication, and journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU recently relocated some nursing and health related programs to its new ASU-Mayo Medical School Campus. Inter-campus shuttles and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> allow students and faculty to easily travel between the campuses. In addition to the physical campuses, ASU's &quot;virtual campus&quot;, housed at the university's <a href="/wiki/Skysong,_the_ASU_Scottsdale_Innovation_Center" title="Skysong, the ASU Scottsdale Innovation Center">SkySong Innovation Center</a>, provides <a href="/wiki/Online_education" title="Online education" class="mw-redirect">online</a> and extended education.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Old_Main.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ASU_Old_Main.jpg/220px-ASU_Old_Main.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ASU_Old_Main.jpg/330px-ASU_Old_Main.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ASU_Old_Main.jpg/440px-ASU_Old_Main.jpg 2x" /></a>

        </div> On the Quad of the Tempe Campus with Old Main

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tempe_campus">Tempe campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tempe campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asu_campus_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asu_campus_1.jpg/250px-Asu_campus_1.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asu_campus_1.jpg/375px-Asu_campus_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asu_campus_1.jpg/500px-Asu_campus_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asu_campus_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Overlooking the Tempe campus from atop 
        <a href="/wiki/Hayden_Butte" title="Hayden Butte" class="mw-redirect">Hayden Butte</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Tempe_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Tempe campus">Arizona State University at the Tempe campus</a>
     </div> 
     <p>ASU's Tempe campus is located in downtown <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe, Arizona</a>, about eight miles (13&nbsp;km) east of downtown Phoenix. The campus is considered urban, and is approximately 642 acres (2.6&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in size. The campus is arranged around broad pedestrian malls and is completely encompassed by an arboretum.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The Tempe campus is also the largest of ASU's campuses, with 59,794<sup id="ref_a" class="reference"><a href="#cnote_a">a[›]</a></sup> students enrolled in at least one class on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-enroll11_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enroll11-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Tempe campus is ASU's original campus, and <a href="/wiki/Old_Main_(Arizona_State_University)" title="Old Main (Arizona State University)">Old Main</a>, the first building constructed, still stands today. There are many notable landmarks on campus, including <a href="/wiki/Grady_Gammage_Memorial_Auditorium" title="Grady Gammage Memorial Auditorium" class="mw-redirect">Grady Gammage Memorial Auditorium</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a>, Palm Walk, which is lined by 111 palm trees,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Charles Trumbull Hayden Library, the University Club Building, and University Bridge. In addition, the campus has an extensive public art collection, considered one of the ten best among university public art collections in America according to <i>Public Art Review</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PAR_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAR-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Against the northwest edge of campus is the Mill Avenue district (part of <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">downtown Tempe</a>) which has a college atmosphere that attracts many students to its restaurants and bars. The Tempe campus is also home to all of the university's athletic facilities.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asuwmain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Asuwmain.jpg/220px-Asuwmain.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Asuwmain.jpg/330px-Asuwmain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Asuwmain.jpg/440px-Asuwmain.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asuwmain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Fletcher Library, West Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_campus">West campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: West campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_West_campus" title="Arizona State University at the West campus">Arizona State University at the West campus</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The West campus was established in 1984 by the Arizona Legislature and sits on 250 acres (1.0&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in a suburban area of northwest Phoenix. The West campus lies about 12 miles (19&nbsp;km) northwest of downtown Phoenix, and about 18 miles (29&nbsp;km) northwest of the Tempe campus. The West campus is designated as a <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Points_of_Pride" title="Phoenix Points of Pride">Phoenix Point of Pride</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Point_of_Pride_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Point_of_Pride-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> and is nearly completely powered by a 4.6<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" title="Megawatt" class="mw-redirect">MW</a> <a href="/wiki/Solar_array" title="Solar array" class="mw-redirect">solar array</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> This campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/New_College_of_Interdisciplinary_Arts_and_Sciences" title="New College of Interdisciplinary Arts and Sciences">New College of Interdisciplinary Arts and Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Fulton_Teachers_College" title="Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College">Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College</a>, and selected programs of the <a href="/wiki/W.P._Carey_School_of_Business" title="W.P. Carey School of Business" class="mw-redirect">W.P. Carey School of Business</a>. The campus, patterned after the University of Oxford’s architecture, has recently opened a new residence hall, dining facility and recreation center.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polytechnic_campus">Polytechnic campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Polytechnic campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg/250px-ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg" width="250" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg/375px-ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg/500px-ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Poly_-_West_-_2009-02-25.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Picacho Hall (left) and Peralta Hall (right) at the Polytechnic campus
       </div> 
      </div>

     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Polytechnic_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Polytechnic campus">Arizona State University at the Polytechnic campus</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Founded in 1996 as &quot;ASU East,&quot; the ASU Polytechnic campus serves 10,521 students and is home to more than 40 bachelor’s, master’s and doctoral degrees in professional and technical programs through the College of Technology and Innovation, and selected programs of the <a href="/wiki/W.P._Carey_School_of_Business" title="W.P. Carey School of Business" class="mw-redirect">W.P. Carey School of Business</a>/Morrison School of Agribusiness and Resource Management, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Fulton_Teachers_College" title="Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College">Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College</a>, the School of Letters and Sciences, and focuses on professional and technological programs including simulators and lab space in various <a href="/wiki/Field_of_study" title="Field of study" class="mw-redirect">fields of study</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-campus.asu.edu_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campus.asu.edu-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The 600-acre (2.4&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) campus is located in southeast <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa, Arizona</a>, approximately 25 miles (40&nbsp;km) southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Tempe_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Tempe campus">Tempe campus</a>, and 33 miles (53&nbsp;km) southeast of downtown Phoenix. The Polytechnic campus sits on the former <a href="/wiki/Williams_Air_Force_Base" title="Williams Air Force Base">Williams Air Force Base</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg/220px-ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg/330px-ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg/440px-ASU_Downtown_-_SoJ_SWC_-_2008-12-29.jpg 2x" /></a>

        </div> Walter Cronkite School of Journalism, Downtown Phoenix Campus

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_Phoenix_campus">Downtown Phoenix campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Downtown Phoenix campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_at_the_Downtown_Phoenix_campus" title="Arizona State University at the Downtown Phoenix campus">Arizona State University at the Downtown Phoenix campus</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The newest of ASU's four campuses, the Downtown Phoenix campus was established in 2006 on the north side of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Phoenix" title="Downtown Phoenix">Downtown Phoenix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus has an <a href="/wiki/Urban_design" title="Urban design">urban design</a>, with several large modern academic buildings intermingled with commercial and retail office buildings. In addition to the new buildings, the campus included the <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_reuse" title="Adaptive reuse">adaptive reuse</a> of several existing structures, including a 1930s era Post Office that is on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. Serving 17,151<sup id="cite_ref-enroll11_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enroll11-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> students, the campus houses the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://healthsolutions.asu.edu/">College of Health Solutions</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nursingandhealth.asu.edu/">College of Nursing and Health Innovation</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASU_College_of_Public_Programs" title="ASU College of Public Programs">College of Public Programs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite_School_of_Journalism_and_Mass_Communication" title="Walter Cronkite School of Journalism and Mass Communication">Walter Cronkite School of Journalism and Mass Communication</a>, and School of Criminology and Criminal Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asupalms.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Asupalms.jpg/220px-Asupalms.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Asupalms.jpg/330px-Asupalms.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Asupalms.jpg/440px-Asupalms.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asupalms.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Palm Walk is frequented by ASU students.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_.40_ASU">Colleges @ ASU</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Colleges @ ASU">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Colleges@ASU" title="Colleges@ASU">Colleges@ASU</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In response to demands for lower-cost public higher education in Arizona, ASU is developing a number of small, undergraduate-only college locations throughout Arizona. Colleges @ ASU locations will be teaching-focused, and will provide a selection of popular undergraduate majors. The first is being planned for <a href="/wiki/Lake_Havasu_City" title="Lake Havasu City" class="mw-redirect">Lake Havasu City</a> with programs available as early as fall 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG/220px-Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG/330px-Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG/440px-Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Music_Auditorium_ASU_Tempe_AZ_220398.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Music Building on the Tempe Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_degree_programs">Online degree programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Online degree programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>ASU offers more than 50 undergraduate and graduate degree programs through an entirely <a href="/wiki/Online_education" title="Online education" class="mw-redirect">online</a> platform, known as ASU Online. The degree programs delivered online hold the same accreditation as the university's traditional face-to-face programs, and students earn many of the same degrees as those who attended courses in person. Online students are taught by the same faculty and receive the same diploma as on-campus students. As of spring 2012, more than 5,000 students were enrolled at ASU Online. ASU Online is headquartered at ASU's <a href="/wiki/Skysong,_the_ASU_Scottsdale_Innovation_Center" title="Skysong, the ASU Scottsdale Innovation Center">SkySong</a> campus in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale</a>, Arizona. ASU Online was ranked #1 in online Student Services and Technology by U.S. News and World Report.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ASU-Mayo_Medical_School_Campus">ASU-Mayo Medical School Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: ASU-Mayo Medical School Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In late 2011, ASU launched a collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Clinic" title="Mayo Clinic">Mayo Clinic</a> to create a medical school.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> As part of the collaboration with Mayo, ASU moved some academic departments onto the Mayo Clinic campus in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Mayo Medical and ASU have instituted an undergraduate &quot;Barrett-Mayo <a href="/wiki/Pre-medical" title="Pre-medical">Pre-medical</a> Scholars Program&quot; to further the ASU Clinical partnering program mission.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> A partnership with organizations and hospitals throughout the region has been created. The partnership will help establish a network for knowledge sharing and testing of innovation. Real-world training for students researching medical issues affecting the community will be a priority of the school.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU-Mayo Medical School plans to begin enrolling the first students in 2014. In preparation for the medical school opening, ASU began offering health and nursing degree programs on the Mayo Clinic Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The program at the ASU-Mayo Clinic Campus began in the Fall of 2012 and provides a <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/hands-on" class="extiw" title="wikt:Special:Search/hands-on">hands-on</a> education in world-class medical facilities to its students.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> After the construction of the school, unique <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a> degrees, believed to be the first in the nation, will be granted under the governance and oversight of <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Medical_School" title="Mayo Medical School">Mayo Medical School</a> and Arizona State University with a specialized <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master’s degree</a> in the Science of <a href="/wiki/Health_systems_management" title="Health systems management">Health Care Management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3>

       </div>

     </div> 
     <p>Admission to any of the public universities in Arizona is ensured to residents in the top 25% of their high-school class with a GPA of 3.0 in core competencies.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012-2013, ASU admitted 87% of all applicants and is considered a &quot;selective&quot; university by U.S. News and World Report.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Average GPA of high school graduates enrolling full-time is 3.42.<sup id="cite_ref-about.asu.edu_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about.asu.edu-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> All freshman are required to live on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Barrett,_The_Honors_College" title="Barrett, The Honors College">Barrett, The Honors College</a> is ranked 1st in the nation among peer institutions (1300-1400 minimum SAT), 4th in Honors Factors, and 5th in Overall Excellence among all universities.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Like most of ASU's colleges and schools (e.g. Walter Cronkite School of Journalism and Mass Communication, W.P. Carey School of Business, Sandra Day O'Connor College of Law, College of Nursing and Health Innovation, etc.),<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Barrett College maintains much more strict admissions standards. Furthermore, Barrett College provides a more rigorous curriculum with smaller classes and increased faculty interaction.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Although there are no set minimum admissions criteria for Barrett College, the average GPA of incoming freshmen was 3.84, with average SAT scores of 1314/1600 and ACT scores of 29.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The Honors college enrolls 3523 undergraduate students, 613 of whom are <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholars" title="National Merit Scholars" class="mw-redirect">National Merit Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU currently enrolls 5,137 <a href="/wiki/International_students" title="International students" class="mw-redirect">international students</a>, 6.1% of the total student population.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The international student body represents 118 nations and more than 60 student clubs and organizations exist at ASU to serve the growing number of students from abroad. The growth in the number of international students in 2012 at ASU is a 16% increase over the 2011 figure.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_programs">Academic programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Academic programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_schools_of_Arizona_State_University" title="List of colleges and schools of Arizona State University">List of colleges and schools of Arizona State University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>ASU offers over 250 majors to undergraduate students, and more than 100 graduate programs leading to numerous <a href="/wiki/Masters_degree" title="Masters degree" class="mw-redirect">masters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral</a> degrees in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts and sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herberger_Institute_for_Design_and_the_Arts" title="Herberger Institute for Design and the Arts">design and arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ira_A._Fulton_School_of_Engineering" title="Ira A. Fulton School of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Journalism" title="Journalism">journalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Fulton_Teachers_College" title="Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_school" title="Business school">business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public policy</a>, technology, and sustainability. These programs are divided into 16 colleges and schools which are spread across ASU's four campuses. ASU uses a plus-minus grading system with highest cumulative GPA awarded of 4.0 (at time of graduation).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>ASU's undergraduate program is ranked 70th for public universities and 139th of 280 &quot;national universities&quot; by the 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/US_News_and_World_Report" title="US News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">US News and World Report</a></i> ranking of US colleges and universities; and, for the fourth year in a row, ASU was ranked in the top 10<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> (4th) for &quot;Up and Coming&quot; universities in the US, for substantial improvements to academics and facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, ASU is ranked 79th in the world / 46th in the US by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and was named as one of &quot;America's Best College Buys&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, &quot;ASU students ranked fifth among all public universities in National Science Foundation grants for graduate study and 11th among all universities, including the Ivy institutions. Among other things, the high achievement in this area of excellence points to consistently strong advising and support, a logical outcome of Barrett (Arizona State University's honor college) investing more in honors staff than any other honors program that&quot; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://publicuniversityhonors.com/2012/05/26/asus-barrett-honors-college-best-value-added-impact-in-the-nation/">Public University Honors</a> reviewed.</p> 
     <p>Arizona State consistently ranks among the top 20 universities—without a traditional medical school—for research expenditures. It shares this designation with schools such as: MIT, UC-Berkeley, Georgia Tech, Texas-Austin, Purdue, Cal Tech and Rockefeller. <sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For its efforts to be a national leader in campus sustainability, ASU was named one of the top 20 &quot;cool schools&quot; by the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">Sierra Club</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> was named to the &quot;Green Honor Roll&quot; by the <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and earned an &quot;A-&quot; grade on the 2010 College Sustainability Report Card.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several of ASU's colleges and schools also appear among the top of the US News &amp; World Report rankings, including the 30th-ranked <a href="/wiki/W._P._Carey_School_of_Business" title="W. P. Carey School of Business">W. P. Carey School of Business</a><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> (along with its 4th-ranked program in <a href="/wiki/Supply_Chain_Management" title="Supply Chain Management" class="mw-redirect">Supply Chain Management</a> and the 15th-ranked program in <a href="/wiki/Information_Systems" title="Information Systems" class="mw-redirect">Information Systems</a>), the 22nd-ranked Herberger Institute for Design and the Arts (Fine Arts),<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> the 12th-ranked School of Criminology and Criminal Justice,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> the 29th-ranked <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Day_O%27Connor_College_of_Law" title="Sandra Day O'Connor College of Law">Sandra Day O'Connor College of Law</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> the 44th-ranked <a href="/wiki/Ira_A._Fulton_School_of_Engineering" title="Ira A. Fulton School of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Ira A. Fulton School of Engineering</a> (including five individual programs ranked in the top 30),<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> the 16th-ranked <a href="/wiki/ASU_School_of_Public_Affairs" title="ASU School of Public Affairs" class="mw-redirect">School of Public Affairs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> the 24th-ranked <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Fulton_Teachers_College" title="Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College">Mary Lou Fulton Teachers College</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> the 21st-ranked <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nursingandhealth.asu.edu/">College of Nursing and Health Innovation</a>, and 25th-ranked Healthcare Management.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the individual Ph.D. programs in <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a> (36th),<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Earth_Science" title="Earth Science" class="mw-redirect">Earth Science</a> (17th),<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">Economics</a> (36th)<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> also earned high rankings. In 2011 ASU made the <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">Quacquarelli Symonds</a> (QS) list as the 21st best school in the world for <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">biological sciences</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Asuhayden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Asuhayden.jpg/250px-Asuhayden.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Asuhayden.jpg/375px-Asuhayden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Asuhayden.jpg/500px-Asuhayden.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Asuhayden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The subterranean entrance to 
        <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://lib.asu.edu/hayden/aboutus">Hayden Library</a>, Tempe campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>ASU's faculty and students are served by two dedicated general-topic libraries: Hayden Library,<sup id="cite_ref-lib.asu.edu_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lib.asu.edu-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> which is the largest of the ASU libraries and is located on the Tempe campus, and Fletcher Library, located on the West campus. In addition, the Ross-Blakley Law Library and the Noble Science Library are housed in dedicated facilities on the Tempe campus. Music and Architecture collections are housed in facilities within the schools of Music and Architecture, respectively. Smaller library facilities are also located on the Polytechnic and Downtown campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2009, ASU's libraries held 4.4 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, there are 7 libraries that service the university community. The Arizona State University library system is ranked the 34th largest research library in the United States and Canada, according to criteria established by the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Research_Libraries" title="Association of Research Libraries">Association of Research Libraries</a> that measures various aspects of quality and size of the collection.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The University continues to grow its rare <a href="/wiki/Special_collections" title="Special collections">special collections</a>, such as the recent addition of a privately held collection of <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscripts</a> by poet <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Dario" title="Ruben Dario" class="mw-redirect">Rub&eacute;n Dar&iacute;o</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Hayden Library is located on Cady Mall in the center of the Tempe campus.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> It opened in 1966 and serves as the library system's reference, periodical, and administrative center and houses the most extensive special collections in ASU’s library system.<sup id="cite_ref-lib.asu.edu_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lib.asu.edu-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> An expansion in 1989 created the subterranean entrance underneath Hayden Lawn and is attached to the above ground portion of the original library. There are two floors underneath Hayden Lawn with a landmark known as the <i>&quot;Beacon of Knowledge&quot;</i> rising form the center. The beacon is lit at night by the underground library’s lights.</p> 
     <p>The 2013 <a href="/wiki/Capital_Improvement_Plan" title="Capital Improvement Plan">Capital Improvement Plan</a>, approved by the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">Arizona Board of Regents</a>, incorporates a $35 million repurposing and renovation project for Hayden Library.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The moat area that is currently open air and serves as an outdoor study space will be enclosed in order to increase indoor space for the library. Along with increasing space and renovating the facility, the front entrance of Hayden Library will be rebuilt.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>As of April 2013, ASU is the only higher education institution in the United States to generate over 20 megawatts (MW) of electricity from <a href="/wiki/Solar_arrays" title="Solar arrays" class="mw-redirect">solar arrays</a>; an increase over the June 2012 total of 15.3 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU has 72 <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_system" title="Photovoltaic system">solar photovoltaic</a> (PV) installations across all four campuses. The largest concentration of solar PV installations are on the Tempe campus, producing over 12.8 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additionally, there are six <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbines" title="Wind turbines" class="mw-redirect">wind turbines</a> installed on the roof of the Global Institute of Sustainability building on the Tempe campus that have been in operation since October 2008. Under normal conditions, the six turbines produce enough electricity to power approximately 36 computers.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU's <a href="/wiki/ASU_School_of_Sustainability" title="ASU School of Sustainability">School of Sustainability</a> is the first school in the United States dedicated to exploring the principles of <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>. The School was established in spring 2007 and began enrolling undergraduates in fall 2008. It is part of the ASU Global Institute of Sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maroon_and_Gold">Maroon and Gold</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Maroon and Gold">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg/220px-Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg/330px-Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg/440px-Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sparky_the_Sun_Devil_vs_USC_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Sparky the Sun Devil with his 
        <a href="/wiki/Trident" title="Trident">trident</a>, 2011
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Gold is the oldest color associated with Arizona State University and dates back to 1896 when the school was named the Tempe Normal School.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Maroon and white were later added to the color scheme in 1898. Gold signifies the “golden promise” of ASU. The promise includes every student receiving a valuable educational experience. Gold also signifies the sunshine Arizona is famous for; including the power of the sun and its influence on the climate and the economy. The first uniforms worn by athletes associated with the university were black and white when the “Normals” were the name of the athletic teams. The student section, known as The Inferno, wears gold on game days.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot_and_Spirit_Squad">Mascot and Spirit Squad</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mascot and Spirit Squad">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sparky_the_Sun_Devil" title="Sparky the Sun Devil">Sparky the Sun Devil</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Sparky_the_Sun_Devil" title="Sparky the Sun Devil">Sparky the Sun Devil</a> is the mascot of Arizona State University and was named by vote of the student body on November 8, 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Sparky often travels with the team across the country and has been at every football <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowl game</a> in which the university has participated in. The university's mascot is not to be confused with the university’s new emblem and logo, The <a href="/wiki/Trident" title="Trident">Trident</a>, colloquially referred to as the <i>fork</i> or the <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(hand_gesture)" title="Pitchfork (hand gesture)">pitchfork</a></i> which is a hand gesture used by those associated with the university. The new logo and emblem are used on various university property, sport facilities, uniforms and documents.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Arizona State Teacher’s College had a different mascot and the sports teams were known as the Owls and later, the Bulldogs. When the school was first established, the Tempe Normal School’s teams were simply known as the Normals.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Sparky is visible on the sidelines of every home game played in <a href="/wiki/Sun_Devil_Stadium" title="Sun Devil Stadium">Sun Devil Stadium</a> or other ASU athletic facilities. His routine at football games includes pushups after every touchdown scored by the Sun Devils. He is aided by Sparky's Crew, male yell leaders that must meet physical requirements in order to participate as members. The female members are known as the Spirit Squad and are categorized into a dance line and spirit line. They are the official squad that represents ASU. The spirit squad competes every year at the ESPN Universal Dance Association (UDA) College Nationals in the Jazz and Hip-Hop categories. They were chosen by the UDA to represent the USA at the World Dance Championship 2013 in the Jazz category.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, ASU's varsity intercollegiate <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a> team is not allowed to participate at athletic events (e.g. football and basketball games) due to dismissal regarding prior misconduct.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU Cheerleading has since become a club sport, through the Student Recreation Center, competing locally and nationally as a Collegiate Co-Ed Division IA-Level VI team. They have reestablished their commitment to excellence, winning various championships.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The team has a strict code of conduct and is seeking reinstatement from the university to participate at athletic events.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain,_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain%2C_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg/220px-Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain%2C_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain%2C_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg/330px-Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain%2C_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Whitewashing_%22A%22_Mountain%2C_Tempe_Butte_on_Arizona_State_University_Campus.jpg 2x" /></a>
