     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".E2.80.9CA.E2.80.9D_Mountain">“A” Mountain</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: “A” Mountain">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tempe_Butte" title="Tempe Butte">Tempe Butte</a>
     </div> 
     <p>A letter has existed on the slope of the mountain since 1918. A &quot;T&quot; followed by an &quot;N&quot; were the first letters to grace the landmark. <a href="/wiki/Tempe_Butte" title="Tempe Butte">Tempe Butte</a>, home to &quot;A&quot; Mountain, has had the &quot;A&quot; installed on the slope of its south face since 1938 and is visible from campus just to the south. The original &quot;A&quot; was destroyed by vandals in 1952 with pipe bombs and a new &quot;A&quot;, constructed of reinforced concrete, was built in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The vandals were never identified but many speculate that the conspirators were students from the rival in-state university (University of Arizona). Many ancient <a href="/wiki/Hohokam" title="Hohokam">Hohokam</a> <a href="/wiki/Petroglyph" title="Petroglyph">petroglyphs</a> were destroyed by the bomb; nevertheless, many of these archeological sites around the mountain remain. There are many traditions surrounding &quot;A&quot; Mountain, including a revived &quot;guarding of the 'A'&quot; in which students camp on the mountainside before games with rival schools.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;Whitewashing&quot; of the &quot;A&quot; is a tradition in which incoming freshmen paint the letter white during orientation week.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> After the painting of the &quot;A&quot;, new students learn the history of ASU and its other traditions.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BatteryPregameCadence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BatteryPregameCadence.jpg/220px-BatteryPregameCadence.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BatteryPregameCadence.jpg/330px-BatteryPregameCadence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BatteryPregameCadence.jpg/440px-BatteryPregameCadence.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BatteryPregameCadence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_Sun_Devil_Marching_Band" title="Arizona State University Sun Devil Marching Band">Sun Devil Marching Band</a> Battery, performing the pregame 
        <a href="/wiki/Drum_cadence" title="Drum cadence">drum cadence</a> in 2007
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lantern_Walk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lantern_Walk.jpg/220px-Lantern_Walk.jpg" width="220" height="587" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lantern_Walk.jpg/330px-Lantern_Walk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Lantern_Walk.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lantern_Walk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Old newspaper clipping describing the Lantern Walk tradition at ASU, May 30, 1929
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lantern_Walk_and_Homecoming">Lantern Walk and Homecoming</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Lantern Walk and Homecoming">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Lantern Walk is one of the oldest traditions at ASU and dates back to 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> It is considered one of ASU’s “most cherished” traditions and is an occasion used to mark the work of those associated with ASU throughout history. Anyone associated with ASU is free to participate in the event, including students, alumni, faculty, employees, and friends. This differs slightly from the original tradition in which the seniors would carry lanterns up &quot;A&quot; Mountain followed by the freshman. The senior class president would describe ASU's traditions and the freshman would repeat an oath of allegiance to the university. It was described as a tradition of &quot;good will between the classes&quot; and a way of ensuring new students would continue the university's traditions with honor. In modern times, the participants walk through campus and follow a path up to “A” Mountain in order to “light up” Tempe. Keynote speakers, performances, and other events are used to mark the occasion. The night is culminated with a fireworks display. The Lantern Walk was held after the Spring Semester (June) but is now held the week before <a href="/wiki/Homecoming" title="Homecoming">Homecoming</a>, a tradition that dates back to 1924 at ASU. It is held in the fall and in conjunction with a football game.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Victory_Bell">Victory Bell</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Victory Bell">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Arizona State University reintroduced the tradition of ringing a bell after each win for the football team in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> The ROTC cadets associated with the university are responsible for the transportation of the bell to various events and for ringing the bell after games are won by the Sun Devils. The first Victory Bell, in various forms, was used in the 1930s but the tradition faded in the 1970s when the bell in use was removed from Memorial Union for renovations.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The bell cracked and was no longer capable of ringing. That bell is located on the southeast corner of Sun Devil Stadium near the entrance to the student section. That bell, gifted to the university in the late 1960s, is painted gold and is a campus landmark today.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sun_Devil_Marching_Band.2C_Devil_Walk_and_Songs_of_the_University">Sun Devil Marching Band, Devil Walk and Songs of the University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sun Devil Marching Band, Devil Walk and Songs of the University">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University_Sun_Devil_Marching_Band" title="Arizona State University Sun Devil Marching Band">Arizona State University Sun Devil Marching Band</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Sun_devil_marching_band" title="Sun devil marching band" class="mw-redirect">The Arizona State University Sun Devil Marching Band</a>, created in 1915 and known as the <i>Pride of the Southwest</i>, was the first of only two <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching bands</a> in the Pac-12 to be awarded the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Sudler_trophy#The_Sudler_Trophy" title="Sudler trophy" class="mw-redirect">Sudler Trophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The John Philip Sousa Foundation awarded the band the trophy in 1991. The Sun Devil Marching Band remains one of only 28 bands in the nation to have earned the designation. The band performs at every football game played in Sun Devil Stadium. Smaller ensembles of band members perform at other sport venues including basketball games at Wells Fargo Arena and baseball games at Packard Stadium. The Devil Walk is held in Wells Fargo Arena by the football team and involves a more formal introduction of the players to the community; a new approach to the tradition added in 2012 with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Head_coach" title="Head coach">head coach</a> Todd Graham.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> It begins 2 hours and 15 minutes prior to the game and allows the players to establish rapport with the fans. The walk ends as the team passes the band and fans lined along the path to Sun Devil Stadium. The most recognizable songs played by the band are <i>Alma Mater</i> and ASU’s <a href="/wiki/Fight_songs" title="Fight songs" class="mw-redirect">fight songs</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Maroon_and_gold" title="Maroon and gold" class="mw-redirect">Maroon and Gold</a></i> and the <i>Al Davis Fight Song</i>. <i>Alma Mater</i> was composed by former Music Professor and Director of Sun Devil Marching Band (then known as Bulldog Marching Band), Miles A. Dresskell, in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Maroon and Gold</i> was authored by former Director of Sun Devil Marching Band, Felix E. McKernan, in 1948. The <i>Al Davis Fight Song</i> (also known as <i>Go, Go Sun Devils</i> and <i>Arizona State University Fight Song</i>) was composed by ASU alum Albert Oliver Davis in the 1940s without any lyrics. Words were recently added to the song.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extracurricular_programs">Extracurricular programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Extracurricular programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Arizona State University has an active <a href="/wiki/Extracurricular" title="Extracurricular" class="mw-redirect">extracurricular</a> involvement program (Sun Devil Involvement Center).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Located on the 3rd floor of the Memorial Union,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> the Sun Devil Involvement Center (SDIC) provides opportunities for student involvement through clubs, <a href="/wiki/Sororities" title="Sororities" class="mw-redirect">sororities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fraternities" title="Fraternities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a>, leadership, <a href="/wiki/Student_government" title="Student government" class="mw-redirect">student government</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Co-curricular_activity" title="Co-curricular activity" class="mw-redirect">co-curricular</a> programming.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Changemaker Central is student-run centralized resource hub for student involvement in <a href="/wiki/Social_entrepreneurship" title="Social entrepreneurship">social entrepreneurship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civic_engagement" title="Civic engagement">civic engagement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Service_learning" title="Service learning" class="mw-redirect">service learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a> that catalyzes student-driven social change. Changemaker Central locations have opened on all campuses in Fall 2011, providing flexible, creative workspaces for everyone in the ASU community. The project is entirely student run and advances ASU’s institutional commitments to social embeddedness and entrepreneurship. The space allows students to meet, work and join new networks and collaborative enterprises while taking advantage of ASU’s many resources and opportunities for engagement.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Changemaker Central has signature programs, including Innovation Challenge and 10,000 Solutions, that support students in their journey to become changemakers by creating communities of support around new solutions/ideas and increasing access to early stage seed funding.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> The Innovation Challenge seeks undergraduate and graduate students from across the university who are dedicated to making a difference in our local and global communities through innovation. Students can win up to $10,000 to make their innovative project, prototype, venture or community partnership ideas happen.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> The 10,000 Solutions Project leverages the power of collaborative imagination and innovation to create a solutions bank. As an experimental problem solving platform, the project showcases and collects ideas at scale with local and global impact. The 10,000 Solutions Project aims to see what can be accomplished when passionate people join a collaborative community that builds upon each other’s innovative ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition to Changemaker Central, the Freshman Year Residential Experience (FYRE) and the <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">Greek</a> community (Greek Life) at Arizona State University have been important in binding students to the university, and providing social outlets. The Freshman Year Residential Experience at Arizona State University was developed to improve the freshman experience at Arizona State University and increase student retention figures. FYRE provides advising, computer labs, free walk-in tutoring, workshops, and classes for students. In 2003, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> ranked FYRE as the 23rd best first year program in the nation. ASU is also home to one of the nation's first and fastest growing gay fraternities, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Beta" title="Sigma Phi Beta">Sigma Phi Beta</a>, founded in 2003;<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> considered a sign of the growing university's commitment to supporting diversity and inclusion.</p> 
     <p>The second Eta chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a>, a non-exclusive, non-profit social-service club, was installed here in 1958. Between 1924 and 1967, 23 chapters of Phrateres were installed in universities across North America.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i>The <a href="/wiki/State_Press" title="State Press">State Press</a></i> is a daily paper published on Monday through Friday during the fall and spring semesters, and weekly during the summer sessions. The State Press covers news and events on all four ASU campuses. Student editors and managers are solely responsible for the content of the State Press newspaper and its associated website. These publications are overseen by an independent board and guided by a professional adviser employed by the University.</p> 
     <p><i>The Downtown Devil</i> is another student-run newspaper with an associated website for the Downtown Phoenix Campus, produced by students at the <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite_School_of_Journalism_and_Mass_Communication" title="Walter Cronkite School of Journalism and Mass Communication">Walter Cronkite School of Journalism and Mass Communication</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU has two radio stations. <a href="/wiki/KASC_(AM)" title="KASC (AM)">KASC</a> The Blaze 1330 AM, is a broadcast station that is owned and funded by the Cronkite School of Journalism, and is completely student-run save for a faculty and professional adviser. The Blaze broadcasts local, alternative and independent music 24 hours a day, and also features news and sports updates at the top and bottom of every hour.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> W7ASU is an <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> station that was first organized in 1935. W7ASU has about 30 members that enjoy amateur radio, and is primarily a <a href="/wiki/Contesting" title="Contesting">contesting</a> club.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Associated Students of Arizona State University (ASASU) is the <a href="/wiki/Student_government" title="Student government" class="mw-redirect">student government</a> at Arizona State University.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> It is composed of the Undergraduate Student Government and the Graduate &amp; Professional Student Association (GPSA). Members and officers of ASASU are elected annually by the student body.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Residence_Hall_Association" title="Residence Hall Association" class="mw-redirect">Residence Hall Association</a> (RHA) of Arizona State University is the student government for every ASU student living on-campus. Each ASU campus has an RHA that operates independently of each other. The purpose of RHA is to enhance the quality of residence hall life and provide a cohesive voice for the residents by addressing the concerns of the on-campus populations to university administrators and other campus organizations; providing cultural, diversity, educational, and social programming; establishing and working with individual hall councils.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Sun_Devils" title="Arizona State Sun Devils">Arizona State Sun Devils</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg/250px-USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg/375px-USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg/500px-USC_vs_ASU_2011.jpg 2x" /></a>

     <p>Arizona State University's <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I" class="mw-redirect">Division I</a> athletic teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Sun_Devils" title="Arizona State Sun Devils">Sun Devils</a>, which is also the nickname used to refer to students and alumni of the university. They compete in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pac-12 Conference</a> in 20 varsity sports. Historically, the university has highly performed in men's, women's, and mixed <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a>; men's, women's, and mixed <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>; women's <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>; women's <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>; <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>; and football. Arizona State University's <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I-A" title="NCAA Division I-A" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Division I-A</a> program competes in 9 varsity sports for men and 11 for women. ASU's current athletic director is Steve Patterson, who was appointed to the position in 2012 after <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Love_(coach)" title="Lisa Love (coach)">Lisa Love</a>, the former Senior Associate Athletic Director at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>, was relieved of her duties.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Love was responsible for the hiring of coaches <a href="/wiki/Herb_Sendek" title="Herb Sendek">Herb Sendek</a>, the men's basketball coach, and <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Erickson" title="Dennis Erickson">Dennis Erickson</a>, the men's football coach.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Erickson was fired in 2011 and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Todd_Graham" title="Todd Graham">Todd Graham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ASU has won 23 national collegiate team championships in the following sports: baseball (5), men's golf (2), women's golf (7), men's gymnastics (1), softball (2), men's indoor track (1), women's indoor track (2), men's outdoor track (1), women's outdoor track (1), and wrestling (1).<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In September 2009 criticism over the seven-figure salaries earned by various coaches at Arizona's public universities (including ASU) prompted the Arizona Board of Regents to re-evaluate the salary and benefit policy for athletic staff.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> With the 2011 expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>, a new $3 billion contract for revenue sharing among all the schools in the conference was established.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> With the infusion of funds, the salary issue and various athletic department budgeting issues at ASU were addressed. The Pac-12's new media contract with <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> allowed ASU to hire a new coach in 2012. A new salary and bonus package (maximum bonus of $2.05 million) was instituted and is one of the most lucrative in the conference.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU also plans to expand its athletic facilities with a <a href="/wiki/Public-private" title="Public-private" class="mw-redirect">public-private investment</a> strategy to create an amateur sports district that can accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a> and operate as an <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Training_Center" title="Olympic Training Center" class="mw-redirect">Olympic Training Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The athletic district will include a $300 million renovation of Sun Devil Stadium that will include new football facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Press_box" title="Press box">press box</a> and football offices in Sun Devil Stadium were remodeled in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Sun_Devils_football" title="Arizona State Sun Devils football">Arizona State Sun Devils football</a> was founded in 1897 under coach <a href="/wiki/Fred_Irish" title="Fred Irish" class="mw-redirect">Fred Irish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, the team has played in the 2012 Fight Hunger Bowl, the 2011 Las Vegas bowl, and the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Bowl" title="Holiday Bowl">Holiday Bowl</a>. The Sun Devils played in the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> and won the Rose Bowl in 1987. The team has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Bowl" title="Fiesta Bowl">Fiesta Bowl</a> in 1983, 1977, 1975, 1973, 1972, and 1971 winning 5 of 6. In 1970 and 1975 they were champions of the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_National_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I FBS National Football Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Division I FBS National Football Championship</a>. The Sun Devils were Pac-12 Champions in 1986, 1996, and 2007. Altogether, the football team has 17 Conference Championships and has participated in a total of 26 bowl games as of 2012.</p> 
     <p>The university also participates in the American Collegiate Hockey Association (ACHA) and is billed as the top program within that league.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in 2013, ASU will be a founding member of the new <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_League" title="Western Collegiate Hockey League">Western Collegiate Hockey League</a> (WCHL). ASU Sun Devils Hockey will compete with NCAA Division 1 schools for the first time in 2012, largely due to the success of the program.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>Arizona State University has produced over 300,000 alumni worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has produced many notable figures over its 125-year history, including: U.S. Senator Carl Hayden (who was instrumental in the growth of Central Arizona including the metropolitan regions of Phoenix and Tucson), <a href="/wiki/Barry_Goldwater,_Jr." title="Barry Goldwater, Jr.">Barry Goldwater, Jr.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Star" title="Silver Star">Silver Star</a> recipient, <a href="/wiki/Pat_Tillman" title="Pat Tillman">Pat Tillman</a>. Other noted alumni include current U.S. Congressional Representatives <a href="/wiki/Ed_Pastor" title="Ed Pastor">Ed Pastor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Mitchell" title="Harry Mitchell">Harry Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrsten_Sinema" title="Kyrsten Sinema">Kyrsten Sinema</a> (the first openly bisexual person elected to Congress), among others; <a href="/wiki/Eric_Crown" title="Eric Crown">Eric Crown</a>, CEO and co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Insight_Enterprises" title="Insight Enterprises">Insight Enterprises, Inc.</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ira_A._Fulton" title="Ira A. Fulton">Ira A. Fulton</a>, philanthropist and founder of Fulton Homes; Craig Weatherup, former Chairman of <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a>; <a href="/wiki/Kate_Spade" title="Kate Spade">Kate Spade</a>, namesake and co-Founder of <a href="/wiki/Kate_Spade_New_York" title="Kate Spade New York">Kate Spade New York</a>; Larry Carter, CFO of <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Smith_(American_politician)" title="Scott Smith (American politician)">Scott Smith</a>, former businessman and current mayor of the <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Az" title="Mesa, Az" class="mw-redirect">City of Mesa</a>. ASU's contributions to sport include numerous Hall of Famers, among them: <a href="/wiki/Phil_Mickelson" title="Phil Mickelson">Phil Mickelson</a> (golf), <a href="/wiki/Danny_White" title="Danny White">Danny White</a> (football), and <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> (baseball).</p> 
     <p>Famous celebrities include: actor <a href="/wiki/David_Spade" title="David Spade">David Spade</a>; actress and singer <a href="/wiki/Lynda_Carter" title="Lynda Carter">Lynda Carter</a>; and national TV host <a href="/wiki/Steve_Allen" title="Steve Allen">Steve Allen</a>. Influential writers and novelists include: <a href="/wiki/Allison_DuBois" title="Allison DuBois">Allison Dubois</a>, whose novels and work with various law enforcement agencies inspired the TV <a href="/wiki/Miniseries" title="Miniseries">miniseries</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Medium_(TV_series)" title="Medium (TV series)">Medium</a></i>; novelist <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Brown_(novelist)" title="Amanda Brown (novelist)">Amanda Brown</a>; filmmaker and screenwriter <a href="/wiki/John_Hughes_(filmmaker)" title="John Hughes (filmmaker)">John Hughes</a>, who is responsible for various Hollywood blockbusters (e.g. <a href="/wiki/National_Lampoon%27s_Vacation" title="National Lampoon's Vacation">National Lampoon's Vacation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferris_Bueller%27s_Day_Off" title="Ferris Bueller's Day Off">Ferris Bueller's Day Off</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weird_Science_(film)" title="Weird Science (film)">Weird Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Breakfast_Club" title="The Breakfast Club">The Breakfast Club</a>, <a href="/wiki/Some_Kind_of_Wonderful_(film)" title="Some Kind of Wonderful (film)">Some Kind of Wonderful</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_candles" title="Sixteen candles" class="mw-redirect">Sixteen Candles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pretty_in_pink" title="Pretty in pink" class="mw-redirect">Pretty in Pink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Planes,_Trains_and_Automobiles" title="Planes, Trains and Automobiles">Planes, Trains and Automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_(film)" title="Beethoven (film)">Beethoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Buck" title="Uncle Buck">Uncle Buck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Career_Opportunities_(film)" title="Career Opportunities (film)">Career Opportunities</a>, <a href="/wiki/101_Dalmatians_(1996_film)" title="101 Dalmatians (1996 film)">101 Dalmatians</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Home_Alone" title="Home Alone">Home Alone</a> series); and best-selling author and Doctor of Animal Science <a href="/wiki/Temple_Grandin" title="Temple Grandin">Temple Grandin</a>, whose work inspired the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Temple_Grandin_(film)" title="Temple Grandin (film)">Temple Grandin</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Claire_Danes" title="Claire Danes">Claire Danes</a>. Journalists and commentators include: <a href="/wiki/Al_Michaels" title="Al Michaels">Al Michaels</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a>' <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" title="Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect">play-by-play commentator</a> including the <a href="/wiki/NFL" title="NFL" class="mw-redirect">National Football League</a>'s broadcast of <i><a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Football" title="Monday Night Football">Monday Night Football</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Dumas" title="Jerry Dumas">Jerry Dumas</a>, writer, essayist, cartoonist, and a columnist for the <i><a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Time_(newspaper)" title="Greenwich Time (newspaper)">Greenwich Time</a></i> and best known for his <i><a href="/wiki/Sam_and_Silo" title="Sam and Silo">Sam and Silo</a></i> comic strip.</p> 
     <p>Among American research universities, Arizona State is ranked 4th for total recipients of the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_scholarship" title="Fulbright scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Fulbright Scholarship</a> in the 2012-2013 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> ASU has made this list more than 3 consecutive years. ASU alumni and students are also noted for their service to the community and have officially been recognized as a top university for contributing to the public good.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> The Arizona State University Alumni Association is located on the Tempe campus in <a href="/wiki/Old_Main_(Arizona_State_University)" title="Old Main (Arizona State University)">Old Main</a>. The Alumni Association is responsible for continuing many of the traditions of the university.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg/220px-Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg/330px-Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg/440px-Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize_2009-Press_Conference_KVA-30.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Elinor Ostrom
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>ASU faculty have included former <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> host <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Brown" title="Aaron Brown">Aaron Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">meta-analysis</a> developer <a href="/wiki/Gene_V._Glass" title="Gene V. Glass">Gene V. Glass</a>, feminist and author <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Feldt" title="Gloria Feldt">Gloria Feldt</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Davies" title="Paul Davies">Paul Davies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ants" title="The Ants">The Ants</a></i> author <a href="/wiki/Bert_H%C3%B6lldobler" title="Bert H&ouml;lldobler">Bert H&ouml;lldobler</a>. <a href="/wiki/Donald_Johanson" title="Donald Johanson">Donald Johanson</a>, who discovered the 3.18 million year old fossil hominid <a href="/wiki/Lucy_(Australopithecus)" title="Lucy (Australopithecus)">Lucy (Australopithecus)</a> in Ethiopia, is also a professor at ASU, as well as <a href="/wiki/George_Poste" title="George Poste">George Poste</a>, Chief Scientist for the <a href="/wiki/Complex_adaptive_system" title="Complex adaptive system">Complex Adaptive Systems</a> Initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Current <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureate" title="Nobel laureate" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureate</a> faculty include <a href="/wiki/Leland_Hartwell" title="Leland Hartwell" class="mw-redirect">Leland Hartwell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_C._Prescott" title="Edward C. Prescott">Edward C. Prescott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 12, 2012 <a href="/wiki/Elinor_Ostrom" title="Elinor Ostrom">Elinor Ostrom</a>, ASU's third Nobel laureate, died at the age of 78.</p> 
     <p>ASU faculty's achievements as of 2012 include:<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>2 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" title="Nobel laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureates</a></li> 
      <li>3 members of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a></li> 
      <li>27 <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy members</a></li> 
      <li>6 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners</li> 
      <li>5 <a href="/wiki/Sloan_Research_Fellow" title="Sloan Research Fellow" class="mw-redirect">Sloan Research Fellows</a></li> 
      <li>25 <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellows" title="Guggenheim Fellows" class="mw-redirect">Guggenheim Fellows</a></li> 
      <li>114 <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Program" title="Fulbright Program">Fulbright American Scholars</a></li> 
      <li>1 <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur Fellow</a></li> 
      <li>11 Members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a></li> 
      <li>65 <a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_AAAS" title="Fellow of the AAAS">American Association for the Advancement of Science Fellows</a></li> 
      <li>2 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a></li> 
      <li>8 <a href="/wiki/PECASE" title="PECASE" class="mw-redirect">Presidential Early Career Awards for Scientists and Engineers</a></li> 
      <li>86 <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">NSF</a> CAREER award winners <sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>8 <a href="/wiki/American_Council_of_Learned_Societies" title="American Council of Learned Societies">American Council of Learned Societies Fellows</a></li> 
      <li>21 <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Fellow" title="IEEE Fellow">IEEE Fellows</a></li> 
      <li>19 <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Prize" title="Humboldt Prize">Alexander Von Humboldt Foundation Prize Winners</a></li> 
      <li>1 Recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Fellowship#Early_grants_and_connections" title="Rockefeller Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">Rockefeller Fellowship</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Arizona_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p><span id="cnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^</a></b></span>&nbsp;<b>a:</b>&nbsp;Campus emrollment figures at ASU are defined by the number of students taking at least one course offered by a department housed on a particular campus. Students who are enrolled in classes on more than one campus (estimated to be 27,484) are counted within each campus's total.<br /></p> 
     <p><span id="cnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^</a></b></span>&nbsp;<b>b:</b>&nbsp;ASU is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_colleges_and_universities_by_enrollment" title="List of United States colleges and universities by enrollment">largest research university in the US</a> under a single administration (one President, Provost, VPs, etc.). In addition ASU's Tempe campus is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_university_campuses_by_enrollment" title="List of United States university campuses by enrollment">largest single university campus</a> in the US.<br /></p>
